National Government Order to the Executive Yuan

Prohibition of Arbitrary Tax Increases in Provinces 73

The National Government yesterday instructed the Executive Yuan, stating that the Ministries of Finance and Industry and Commerce have jointly submitted a report stating, "We earnestly request a nationwide order to be issued to prevent local areas from arbitrarily increasing taxes and levies, in order to maintain financial stability and protect industry and commerce."

We believe that the key to realizing the principles of the People's Livelihood is to prioritize the development of domestic industry and commerce. The key to reorganizing national finances is to first unify revenue and expenditure procedures. In order to reorganize finances and protect the people's livelihood, the central government, on November 20th of the 17th year, issued an order dividing national and local revenue, clearly stipulating that likin and all similar taxes on transit similar to likin, would be centrally controlled, and strictly prohibiting local surcharges. Furthermore, on January 17th of this year, the government issued another clear order that all likin and similar taxes across the country would be abolished starting from October 10th. This was intended to establish standardized collection methods, so that finances could be reorganized, and to eliminate excessive and miscellaneous taxes, so that there would be hope for the development of industry and commerce. Once industry and commerce thrive,

the tax base will be robust, financial resources will be abundant, government affairs will be managed effectively, and the national economy and people's livelihood will both benefit. However, since the 17th year and thereafter, although orders have been issued, various localities have not complied and have arbitrarily imposed surcharges, which are prevalent everywhere.

The onerousness of their names and the multiplicity of checkpoints cause industry and commerce to be hampered by extortion and obstruction, and finance to be in a state of confusion and divergence.

If this is not promptly eliminated, how can the central government's policies of managing finances and enriching the people be realized? The ministries in charge of industry, commerce, and finance should uphold the central government's intentions, and earnestly comply with the plans to alleviate the hardships of industry and commerce and reorganize finances. Previously, business associations, merchants, and factories in various provinces, counties, and cities had submitted requests to eliminate excessive and miscellaneous taxes to alleviate their difficulties, such as the Joint Association of Ramie Fabric Traders from Sichuan and Shanxi in Shanghai.

For each piece of ramie fabric with a value of around thirty-seven yuan, the journey from Rongchang, Sichuan, to Chongqing, is only three hundred li, but the taxes paid, excluding regular taxes, include as many as fifteen different miscellaneous taxes. For example, nine cents for the postal pavilion protection fee, 27.5 cents for the Jin Yong Lu protection fee, 7.5 cents for the Jin Yong Lu group fee, 10 cents for the Da'an Chang stamp tax, 10 cents for the Ma Fang Bridge mountain defense fee, 24 cents for the Xiao Ma Fang Bridge mountain defense fee, 8 cents for the Lai Feng Post protection stamp fee, 12.5 cents for the Yu Bei protection fee, 12.5 cents for the Yu Bei river defense fee, 8.125 cents for the Yu Bei sub-collection fee, 10 cents for the Yu Bei stamp fee,

30 cents for the Chongqing unified tax, 12 cents for the Chongqing unified tax surcharge,

7.25 cents for the Chongqing protection fee, and 2.4 cents for the Chongqing business group fee, totaling more than 1.9 yuan. Upon entering Yichang, an additional 28.9 cents for the levee construction fee is added, bringing the total to more than 2.196 yuan. If the regular taxes to be paid are added, the tax rate, based on the principal, reaches 8 to 9 percent.

This is only the case for the journey from Rongchang to Yichang, which is already so burdensome. Furthermore, according to a report from the Danhua Match Company forwarded by the Beijing Municipal Government, the unified tax form for machine-made imitation foreign goods originated in the late Qing Dynasty and clearly stated that no further taxes would be levied after the regular tax was paid. Since the establishment of the Republic of China,

this practice has been continued and regarded as the primary policy to benefit industry. In recent years, each province and region has acted independently, and the unified tax form has lost its effectiveness.

In the summer of the 18th year, the factory association of this city submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to maintain the unified tax system. The Ministry approved the request and ordered compliance, but the heavy taxation in various provinces and regions remains the same as before. Taking the match industry as an example, each small package of 2,400 small boxes weighs less than 35 catties and costs less than six yuan to produce on average. When transported to Suiyuan, in addition to the unified tax, the Xizhimen Railway Station in Beijing charges 10 cents for the grain and cargo unified tax, Zhangjiakou charges 36.4 cents for the Da You tax, 22 cents for the bandit suppression tax, Gui Sui charges 37.8 cents for the cargo tax, and the Sai Bei entrance and exit tax is 4.48 cents each. Suiyuan charges 7.57 cents for the Qing Yuan Bureau tax, totaling 1.2273 yuan in double taxation. When transported to Henan, in addition to the unified tax, the Xibianmen Railway Station in Beijing charges 10 cents for the Hebei tax, and Shijiazhuang charges 27.55 cents for the unified tax, totaling 37.55 cents in double taxation. Local landing fees, military contributions, surcharges, and station fees collected with freight are not included. This obstructs industry, the people's livelihood, and government orders deeply and significantly. Therefore, we request that the government forward the situation to the central government, promptly and strictly maintain the unified tax system, and ensure tangible benefits. The departments have carefully reviewed the taxes paid by the company and found that the tax rate, including the unified tax, reaches 22 to 23 percent for goods transported to Suiyuan and 8 to 9 percent for goods transported to Henan. In addition, according to investigations by the departments, transporting porcelain from Jingdezhen, Jiangxi, to Beijing costs no more than 30 yuan per load. In addition to the one yuan of regular tax paid in Jingdezhen, another 20 cents has recently been added. Along the way, taxes must be paid in various places such as Hukou, Huayang, Wuhu, Dasheng Pass, and Sancha River, totaling about 1.23 yuan. If the regular tax and its surcharges are combined, the tax rate also reaches 8 to 9 percent.

In summary, the tax burden in the inland provinces

is unparalleled. Although the specific tax burden varies for other factories and businesses due to different sales markets, one example can represent the rest. It is no wonder that domestic industry and commerce are difficult to revitalize, and finance is difficult to unify. The reason for this is that

local areas have failed to comply with government orders and have arbitrarily imposed surcharges. In order to realize the central government's policies of managing finances and enriching the people, we dare to jointly submit this report to the government, earnestly requesting that the order to abolish likin issued on January 17th of this year be promoted and expanded throughout the country. According to the central government's decision, all goods and tax revenues have been designated as state-owned. Regardless of whether the central government has levied taxes or not, each province and city must not arbitrarily collect taxes or increase surcharges to further burden the people.

During the period before the actual abolition of likin, we also earnestly request that the provincial and municipal governments and relevant departments devise methods to prohibit local establishment of checkpoints, restrict surcharges, and abolish excessive taxes that violate departmental regulations, and report back for review and enforcement.

in order to eliminate abuses and ensure implementation. In addition to jointly submitting another document to the Executive Yuan, earnestly requesting review and enforcement, we hereby submit this document to your office for review, and we humbly request approval for implementation, etc. This should be approved. In addition to the instructions, the Executive Yuan is hereby ordered to immediately instruct compliance and report back as necessary.

Communist Resurgence in Western Fujian 74

Capture of Zhangping and Other Counties

Party Headquarters Telegraphs to Beijing for Assistance

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since the transfer of Liu Heding's division and the departure of Jin Handing's division, the twenty counties in the Tingzhou, Zhangzhou, and Longyan prefectures of western Fujian have been left with only Zhang Zhenyi's army stationed for defense. However, Zhang's army also dispatched a regiment to Chaozhou and Shantou, leaving the military force weak and the defenses empty. Therefore, the communists seized the opportunity to rise again.

They established the Western Fujian Soviet Government in the Ninth Middle School in Longyan County, appointed a person named Kui Zihui as chairman, gathered a crowd of five to six thousand bandits, and captured the counties of Zhangping, Hua'an, Shanghang, Yongding, Liancheng, Nan'an, and Pinghe. They are now divided into two routes, one advancing from Liancheng and Shanghang to Tingzhou, seeking to enter northern Fujian, and the other advancing from Nan'an and Zhangping to Zhangzhou, seeking to enter southern Fujian. For a time, half of the downstream region was shaken. The provincial government has been receiving urgent telegrams from various counties requesting assistance every day, and it is almost impossible to cope with them. Currently, only

Zhang Zhen's division has been ordered to defend Zhangzhou and suppress the bandits in Zhangping and Nan'an, and Lu Xingbang's division has been ordered to defend Tingzhou and suppress the bandits in Liancheng and Shanghang. At the same time, another telegram has been sent to the National Government to request instructions on how to proceed. Yesterday, according to a telegram from Division Commander Zhang,

Zhangzhou has declared a state of special martial law, and the local area is still peaceful and can be secured. Division Commander Lu also telegraphed that he had ordered Huang Qingcai and Lu Xinming's regiments to defend Tingzhou. However, due to the lack of

troops in the captured counties, it is difficult to recover them for the time being. During the communist occupation, they implemented their communist policies, forcing young men and women to serve as Red Guards and propagandists, evenly distributing land, burning deeds, confiscating capital, and destroying production, devastating the social and economic foundations. This is truly heartbreaking. The provincial party committee also believes that if they do not plan to eliminate them as soon as possible, it will inevitably affect the overall situation. Therefore, they sent separate telegrams to the General Headquarters and the Ministry of Military Affairs, stating

"Western Fujian has suffered from communist disaster for more than a year. Since the provincial changes, the troops suppressing the communists have been transferred to distant locations one after another, causing the communist bandits to spread and the overall situation to become critical. We humbly request that you quickly send a strong force to Fujian day and night,

cooperate in suppressing them, so that they can be eliminated as soon as possible," etc. It is unknown how the General Headquarters will handle this telegram. (April 7th)

Suiyuan Implements Spring Planting Subsidies 75

Disaster Relief Committee Stipulates Loan Measures

Suiyuan Correspondence: The Suiyuan Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, due to the spring planting seeds,

purchased them properly in Xuanhua, Datong, and other places. Due to the lack of vehicles on the Ping Sui Railway, they could not be transported back. It was proposed that 50,000 yuan of the funds originally intended for purchasing seeds be loaned to disaster-stricken households in various counties to arrange for their own transportation to avoid delaying the farming season. Later, it was increased by 50,000 yuan, and now it has been increased by another 52,000 yuan. Together with the seeds purchased a few days ago that will be transported soon, more than 3,000 shih of Millet and 100 shih of Grain will be allocated and loaned together. In total, this loan of grain and funds, excluding the counties of Wuyuan and Linhe, where the disaster situation is very light and will not be distributed, will be distributed to more than 186,000 yuan in the 15 counties under the jurisdiction of Guisui. The Disaster Relief Committee's deposit, excluding those designated for labor relief in various counties, is almost entirely allocated for this loan. It is said that the standards for loans have been assigned to the county magistrates to accurately investigate the disaster-stricken conditions of the households

and determine the amount of the loan. It should not be like

the past, where it was distributed evenly among various districts and villages. However, in order to conform to the original intention of subsidizing seeds

and ensure repayment, it is still limited to households with land. The loan measures set by the committee are disclosed below:

(Article 1) This committee has stipulated measures for the purpose of subsidizing autumn planting as a criterion for lending grain and funds. (Article 2) The loan amount of this committee is 152,000 yuan, and the loan amount of grain is the amount of Millet and Grain received in the five counties of Linhe. (3,284

Shih of millet, 100 Shih of grain) (Article 3) The millet in the previous article is priced at 11 yuan per shih, and the grain is priced at 10 yuan per shih, as the standard for future repayment. (Article 4)

The grain and funds loaned by this committee should be repaid in full in the form of funds after autumn. (Article 5) The millet loaned by this committee should be allocated to counties suitable for planting, and counties that are not suitable should be loaned with funds. (Article 6) The grain and funds loaned by this committee should be allocated according to the disaster situation in each county, and the amount to be received is as follows: 25,900 yuan for Guisui County, 10,500 yuan for Tuo County, 16,000 yuan for Sa County, 15,000 yuan for Wuchuan County, 5,200 yuan for Helin County, 10,000 yuan for Baotou County, 9,000 yuan for Guyang County, 2,600 yuan for Dongsheng County, 22,000 yuan for Fengzhen County, 26,000 yuan for Jining County, 13,500 yuan for Liangcheng County, 10,000 yuan for Taolin County, 15,800 yuan for Xinghe County, 3,100 yuan for Dashetai Set-up Bureau, and 2,000 yuan for Qingshuihe County. The above 15 counties and bureaus total

186,600 yuan. (Article 7) The county magistrates of each county are fully responsible for the loan and collection of funds by this committee. (Article 8) After receiving the loan, the county magistrates should give priority to allocating it to the districts and villages under their jurisdiction that are most severely affected by the disaster, but they are not allowed to lend it to households without land in order to comply with the purpose of subsidizing autumn planting. (Article 9)

The village heads and deputy heads of each district and village should be fully responsible for the loan and collection of funds. (Article 10) The amount of grain and funds borrowed by local households should be limited to the needs of two qing of land to prevent the abuse of monopoly by large households.

(Article 11) The amount of grain and funds borrowed by local households should be mortgaged with a contract for immovable property that is three times the amount of the loan, but it is also the same when there are other equivalent guarantees. (Article 12) The grain and funds borrowed by local households should be converted into cash by themselves after autumn and handed over to the county magistrate by the village heads and deputy heads for collection, but it must not be later than the Beginning of Winter Festival. (Article 13) After receiving the funds in the previous article, the county magistrates should submit them to the committee in batches for verification and collection. (Article 14)

The county magistrates should be responsible for supervising the repayment of loans by local households. (Article 15) Local households that fail to repay the loans on time shall be subject to a late payment fee of 10 percent, but it shall not be later than the Winter Solstice Festival. (Article 16) If local households fail to repay the loans by the Winter Solstice Festival, the mortgaged property shall be auctioned off or other guarantees shall be enforced. (Article 17) The county magistrates who fail to handle this case effectively shall be punished by the Provincial Government upon request by the Committee. (

Article 18) These measures shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Congress.

Guangdong Province Sends Troops to Northern Guangdong to Suppress Communists 76

Counties such as Nanxiong and Shixing are Captured by Zhu De and Peng Dehuai Successively

The Authorities Send Six Regiments of Troops to Encircle and Suppress the Communists in Northeastern Guangdong

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the communist bandits in the Gan border ravaged more than ten counties in southern Jiangxi, Zhu De, Peng Dehuai, Liu Guangxia

were divided into three groups to disturb northern Guangdong after the Jiangxi army went south to suppress them. Initially, due to the emptiness of the defense army in southern Jiangxi, the communist bandits fled south in two groups. Liu Guangxia's group fled to Changning in eastern Jiangxi, (that is, Xunwu). On the 24th of last month, Liu led Gu Bai, Zhong Ximiao, and others to capture Chengjiang Market near Xunwu. Xie Jiayou, the head of the Xunwu militia, led his troops to meet them. Xunwu was in extreme danger, so they telegraphed to the Guangdong border defense army for assistance. Mao Weishou, the commander of the 8th Brigade stationed in the Dongjiang area, heard the news and immediately dispatched the 4th Company to Pingyuan and sent Battalion Commander Feng to lead his troops and a machine gun platoon to Xunwu to assist the militia in suppressing them. Finally, Liu's group of communist bandits was defeated.

More than thirty red flags were captured, and hundreds of people were captured. Liu Guangxia was killed and his head was cut off. As a result, the communist bandits who fled to eastern Jiangxi

were greatly diminished. Although this group was pacified, Zhu De and Peng Dehuai's two groups suddenly became rampant in the northern Guangdong area. On the 28th of last month, after the communist bandits Zhu De and Mao Zedong captured Nankang, Nanxiong on the Guangdong border was in great danger. The business community telegraphed the province to stop shipping goods, and merchants migrated.

The county soldiers and guards gathered on the border for defense, and at the same time, they asked the province for assistance. The communist bandits saw that the defense army was weak and divided into two groups to attack northern Guangdong.

Zhu De and Mao Zedong's group attacked Renhua, and Peng Dehuai and Zhu Quan's group attacked Nanxiong. The Nanxiong defense army held out against the communist bandits near Gengling for three days. As a result, because the bandit forces were huge and the provincial army could not arrive in time, Nanxiong fell on the 1st of this month. Zhu De and Mao Zedong's group also occupied the Changjiang Fuxi area of western Nanxiong. Since the above-mentioned areas have fallen to the bandits, Shixing is only ninety-five li away from Nanxiong and has no defenses. At that time, only two battalions of the provincial army's Wu regiment had arrived. Shixing County Chief Zhou urgently recruited troops, and the newly arrived two battalions were stationed outside the city. After occupying Nanxiong City on the 1st,

the communist bandits advanced south day and night, directly under the jurisdiction of the Gushi Ma Shi Mayor. The Shixing County Chief took the archives and seals to the province on the 2nd, and the personnel of various agencies and party headquarters also fled to Shaoguan for temporary refuge. On the evening of the 2nd, Zhu De and Peng Dehuai forced the city of Shixing, and the defense army could not resist. Shixing fell to the bandits on the morning of the 3rd. After Shixing was lost, Renhua was also undefended.

Because Zhu De's group went down along Fuxi, the county soldiers could not resist.

After receiving the police reports from Renhua and Shixing, the provincial authorities urgently transferred troops to Shao, heading for the blockade. Peng Linsheng's Fifth-ninth Division Training Regiment and Wu Wenxian's Sixty-third Division Training Regiment (

The first and second battalions of Wu's unit had already joined the Shaoguan sand team of Li Shaoqin and departed for Shixing a few days ago, and now the third battalion of He Ding's unit is leaving under the personal leadership of Wu), Liang Gongfu's Da Wu Battalion, Yi Wenwei's 9th Gendarmerie Team, and a machine gun platoon, departed from the province at 9:00 a.m. on the 3rd by Guangdong-Han Railway. Huang Hangnan's Fifth-ninth Division Supplementary Regiment and Zeng Youren's Third Independent Regiment stationed in Wu, returned to the province from Wu on the 3rd to concentrate and transferred to the northern Guangdong to cooperate in suppressing the bandits. In addition, the provincial government telegraphed Mao Weishou's 8th Brigade in Dongjiang Meixian to leave Xunwu along the Ganbian Anyuan and come out of Longnan to intercept the rear of the Nanxiong Shixing communist bandits. It was found that there were only two to three thousand people in Zhu De and Peng Dehuai's two groups, and it should not be difficult to annihilate them with one drumbeat if the Guangdong province sends six regiments of troops to northern Guangdong to encircle them. (April 5th)

Guangdong Province Plans to Abolish Customs Tonnage Dues Office 77

The Provincial Government Meeting Has Passed, and Will Be Submitted to the Central Government for Approval

Guangzhou Correspondence: The management of Chinese and foreign steamships sailing in our country's ports or inland has always been handled by the Customs Tonnage Dues Office, which actually damages our country's sovereignty, industrial and commercial navigation, as well as national defense and economy.

Deng Yanhua, Director of the Department of Construction, recently proposed to the Provincial Government to forward a request to the National Government to completely abolish the existing Tonnage Dues Office and have the Department consider establishing a Port Affairs Bureau or Shipping Bureau for temporary management, or to merge the Navigation Affairs Bureau to unify authority. The proposal has been resolved by the Provincial Government's 60th meeting to be handled as proposed. The original proposal of Deng is recorded as follows: 1. The management of Chinese and foreign steamships sailing in our country's ports or inland is handled by the Customs Tonnage Dues Office. The buoys, lighthouses, beacons, etc., set up in each port must also be built by the consul in conjunction with the local officials, so that sovereignty is controlled by foreigners, and the national system is lost. Industrial and commercial navigation is restricted, and national defense and economy are also affected. All kinds of disadvantages can be said by everyone. Moreover, since it concerns internal affairs, how can foreigners overstep their authority? Therefore, Qingdao and Shanghai have already prepared to take them back. Guangdong, as the source of the revolution, can it be allowed to feel at ease? Dare to express my humble opinion and elaborate on it. 1. The reasons for taking them back.

The establishment of the Customs Tonnage Dues Office began in the tenth year of Guangxu.

It was realized in the twenty-fourth year of Guangxu. At that time, there were no navigation affairs agencies in the provinces. Robert Hart, the Inspector General of Customs, said that the number of Chinese and foreign small steamships sailing was increasing day by day, and a special chapter on inland ports should be promulgated for management. He made this statement to the Qing court, and the Qing emperor was weak and hastily approved his request, so it has been followed to this day. Today, the situation is different, and it is no longer what it used to be. Navigation affairs bureaus have been set up almost everywhere. If the Tonnage Dues Office is not abolished, the authority of navigation affairs cannot be unified. This is the first point of why it should be taken back and managed. Moreover, our country's property, our country's ships, or foreign

ships, sailing in our country, our country cannot manage them, and the authority is taken from others, which is unheard of in other countries in the world. What is more unfair? Currently, we are actively proceeding with the abolition of unequal treaties. If we abandon the Tonnage Dues Office and ignore it, how can we protect sovereignty and exalt the national system? This is the second point of why it should be taken back and managed. Moreover, port bays and waterways are related to national defense. All independent countries strictly prohibit foreigners from surveying and photographing their territories, and allow them freedom. Where is national defense placed? This is the third point of why it should be taken back and managed. The Tonnage Dues Office is run by foreign officials, who have territorial prejudices. They often make things difficult for Chinese ships, but they are lenient to foreign ships. Chinese merchants feel the difficulty of operating Chinese ships and the ease of operating foreign ships. Therefore, they often transform Chinese ships into foreign ships, and the amount of money paid to foreign countries every year is unknown. The economy has been invaded. Moreover, with the number of foreign ships increasing and the number of Chinese ships decreasing, navigation is declining, and industry and commerce cannot be revitalized. This is the fourth point of why it should be taken back and managed. The Customs is managed by foreigners because it is related to indemnities and debts, but the Tonnage Dues Office manages ships, which is not related to indemnities, and is actually different from the Customs. Abolition is very easy.

This is the fifth point of why it should be taken back. The establishment of buoys, lighthouses, beacons, etc., in commercial ports is mentioned in the Sino-British Treaty of Xianfeng Eight Years.

That is the beginning of the Tonnage Dues Office managing navigational marks. However, other infringed powers, regardless of which treaty, have no explicit provisions. It is actually due to the gradual encroachment and control of the Inspector General of Customs.

Even though the Regulations on Chinese and Foreign Steamships Sailing in Inland Ports were approved by the Qing court, it was a matter of internal affairs. How can it not be abolished by the central government? This is the sixth point of why it should be taken back and managed. In view of the above six reasons, it can be seen that it is urgent to take back navigation rights and manage them ourselves. Currently, it has been found that in Shanghai and Qingdao, the original Tonnage Dues Office has been abolished and replaced by the Port Affairs Bureau. Guangdong Province, as the hub of trade in the South China Sea, should follow the example and do the same. It is proposed that your office forward the request to the National Government to completely abolish the existing Tonnage Dues Office, and at the same time, the Office will consider establishing a Port Affairs Bureau or Shipping Bureau for temporary management, or merging the Navigation Affairs Bureau to unify authority. Whether it is appropriate or not, I respectfully request a public decision. (April 3rd)

Jiangxi Province Extends Deadline for Three Roads to be Completed 78

Recent Situation of Construction on the Three Lines Connecting Zhejiang, Guangdong, and Anhui

The Department Orders the Highway Administration to Speed Up Construction

Nanchang Correspondence: The construction of the three roads in Jiangxi Province, namely Jiangxi-Zhejiang, Jiangxi-Guangdong, and Jiangxi-Anhui (Jinghu Section), was originally scheduled to be completed by the end of March this year. Later, due to the disturbances of the communist bandits and the difficulty in raising funds, the Director of the Highway Administration, Liu, specifically reported the progress of each road to the Department of Construction.

He requested that troops be sent to suppress the bandits so that he could engage in construction, and he also requested permission to extend the completion deadline. It is said that Director Zhang specially ordered him to extend the deadline to the end of June.

To complete all the projects to facilitate transportation. The recent situation of the construction of the three roads is roughly as follows:

Jiangxi-Guangdong Road: The roadbed between Zhangshu and Xingan and within the territory of Ji'an is being stepped up. It happened that a bandit alarm occurred in Xiajiang, a neighboring county, and Xingan was in danger. The road construction workers fled back one after another. When the bandit forces were slightly reduced in December last year,

When work was resumed, the weather was cold and there was rain and snow,

The progress of the road work was extremely slow. As for the section between Xiajiang and Jishui, the communists have been besieging for years, and nine out of ten houses are empty. Those who have a little property have moved to other places to avoid the bandit disaster. Raising funds and dispatching workers are both difficult. In addition, the county has the longest route and the most severe banditry.

The funds for the roadbed to be raised account for the majority, amounting to 120,000 yuan. The orders of the government cannot leave the county gate, and it is difficult to raise even a few thousand yuan. There is a feeling of having no rice to cook.

Jiangxi-Anhui Road: 92 percent of the road in Fuliang within the Jinghu Road has been completed. People in Poyang are very negative about raising funds and dispatching workers because the route is too far from the city. The earthwork cost in Duchang has also been raised as scheduled, and the costs of small wooden bridges and culvert pipes are also being raised. The only reason for the delay is that the local area is unstable and there is too much rain and snow. Hukou is a poor and barren area, and only half of the road funds have been raised. In September last year, the Anhui bandits occupied the route, so the workers did not dare to go to the road to work, and the project was suspended. Jiangxi-Zhejiang Road: In addition to the three counties of Nanchang, Jinxian, and Dongxiang, which have started construction in order, Yugan, Yujiang, Linchuan, Qianshan, Yushan, and other townships will start construction soon. The three counties of Shangrao, Yiyang, and Guixi are unable to raise funds and dispatch workers because the bandit wind is very strong. Even the funds for the road that have been raised have been diverted for bandit suppression. For this reason, in addition to daring not to slack off in the progress of the road work, we will also try our best to increase the earthwork to be completed on each line in order to complete it as soon as possible.

Banditry in Various Counties of Jiaodong 79

Qingdao Dispatch: Since the change in Gao Guizi's troops in Zhucheng, the troops stationed in various places have been transferred to encircle and suppress [them], leaving the defenses empty. Taking advantage of this opportunity, local ruffians colluded with bandits to plunder wantonly. The bandit situation in various counties is explored and recorded as follows:

Jiaoxian: Jiaoxian has been supplying provisions to the stationed troops for years, owing tens of thousands of yuan in public funds. A public welfare bureau was specially established to reorganize [finances].

Since its establishment, the bureau has added a "military post-disaster donation" to the land tax and grain levy, collecting as much as three yuan for every tael of silver. It is found that Jiaoxian levies about 48,000 taels of land tax silver in total.

This post-disaster donation can collect 144,000 yuan. The pursuit is now very urgent, and the people cannot bear the suffering. In addition, with the stationed troops being transferred elsewhere and bandits rampant, murders and arson are heard of every day. There are about ten large and small gangs of bandits. The well-known bandit leaders are Zhu Daheshang, Sun Yuanshan, Li Xiaoqi, and Qi Mai, etc. The large gangs have hundreds of people, and the small gangs also have dozens of people. Since the beginning of spring, more than 200 families have been victimized, and about 60 to 70 people have been killed by bandits. The most tragic victims are the Zhang family in Shuangjing, Dongxiang. All five members of the family were burned to death by bandits.

Zhucheng: Since the Gao (Guizi) and Fan (Xiji) troops opened fire in the county, many civilian houses in the city have been demolished by Gao's troops.

[These houses were] moved to be used as defensive works. The residents who suffered from the shelling are countless. The wealthy households outside the city have long since moved to other places to avoid [the conflict].

Those who could not afford to move were either plundered by bandits or caught by government soldiers to serve as transportation teams. According to those who came to Qingdao from the county to seek refuge,

the villages near the city have been almost completely deserted. The villages a little further from the city are also often subjected to tragedies due to the prevalence of bandits, leaving people in a state where they cannot live and cannot die.

Pingdu: Pingdu is adjacent to Jiaoxian. Large gangs of bandits from Jiaoxian often come to Pingdu to kidnap [people for ransom]. According to investigations, dozens of families in the county have also been kidnapped, with losses of no less than 70,000 to 80,000 yuan. Although the families in various counties who have suffered misfortune have been harmed by bandits, none have reported the cases to the county government, because the official authorities cannot do anything to help, and only incur resentment from the bandits. Therefore, even though they have suffered tragedy, they only blame their own bitter fate. (April 7)

Han Stele Discovered in Outer Mongolia 80

Suiyuan Dispatch: The world knows that the Mongolians are vulgar and uncultured, with a nature close to savagery. However, observing the solemnity and secrecy with which they preserve the mausoleum of Genghis Khan, the Yuan Dynasty leader, even the Ming and Qing imperial tombs may be hard-pressed to match it. Recently, it has been widely rumored that a Han stele has been discovered in Outer Mongolia, which is temporarily considered rare and unheard of. However, it is not known that the Han Dynasty was the most powerful militarily, subjugating the northern regions and dividing [them into] districts and counties. Today's Mongolia was the Xiongnu at that time, and erecting a stele to record achievements is also within expectations. It is heard that the stele is located in the Ordos Sum near Kulun (Mongolians call temples Sum), which is about forty li to the southeast. This Sum is a Yuan Dynasty building, majestic and magnificent, and incomparably brilliant. In the past, the Dalai Lama often came here for pilgrimage. The stele is in front of the temple, inside an octagonal pavilion. This pavilion is similar in shape to the Hall of Prayer for Good Harvests in the old capital, but on a smaller scale, with similar splendor. The stele is about eleven feet high, four feet wide, and the thickness is equal to the width. The stone has golden specks, and it shines brightly when viewed at night. All four sides of the stele have inscriptions, with traces of moss here and there,

and the handwriting is mottled, tall, vigorous and powerful, and the carvings are all skillful. It is indeed a product of the early Han Dynasty. The inscription on the stele is not recorded, but it does contain the words "General of the Agile Cavalry."

During the Qing Dynasty, the Assistant Resident Officer of Uliastai (Zhi Rui) once visited the site and ordered his attendants to make many rubbings, which were distributed to friends and former colleagues upon his return to Beijing. Thirty years have passed since then, and they have long been lost without a trace. If we want to regain the treasure of the Han Dynasty inscriptions, we must wait for the recovery of Outer Mongolia; otherwise, we dare not lightly tour the Yuan capital to observe it. It is heard that the Mongolians call this stele the "Stele God" and preserve it with great effort, sharing incense and paper money with it after the deity is worshiped. The base of the stele only has slight traces of smoke. (April 1)

(3) The workers who had left due to the dispute would be responsible for being called back by the worker representatives. Those who return before April 5 will not be held responsible. There were also slight changes in other bureau members, patrol officers, and employees.

Yangzhou 87

Bandits with guns attempt to rob: Five or six bandits carrying guns were found on Xia Pu Street in this county last night (the 8th), intending to rob a certain family. However, the local people were aware of it and immediately gathered a large crowd to interrogate them.

Seeing that the situation was not good, the bandits immediately fled. At the same time, four or five bandits were also found in Yang'ao Nei, one of whom dared to carry a musket on his back and walk openly. It happened that a police officer from the Second Public Security Branch Bureau passed by and saw that his behavior was suspicious. He returned to the bureau to report, and a team was dispatched to come. The bandits had already fled far away upon hearing the news.

After Yongjiheng went bankrupt, the Yongjiheng Salt Store opened by Zhou Fuqiu, a transport merchant, went bankrupt because of business failures in recent years, and various money houses and banks

successively pressed for payment. Therefore, the store declared bankruptcy a month ago. As a result, the amount of silver owed was more than 1.8 million, and even in Yangzhou alone, there were more than 580,000. It is estimated that the money houses in this city that deal with the salt store are Yufeng, Lichang, Xinyu, Qingda, and Hui.

The number is the largest. However, this matter is very important to the Yangzhou market. Therefore, the Qianzhuang publicly requested Wang Jingting from the Chamber of Commerce to go to Shanghai to seriously negotiate with Zhou Weibin, who is currently in charge of the salt store.

Jingjiang 88

The bandit disaster in Siyang is intensifying: Siyang has always been known as an area with many bandits, and recently it has been especially rampant. Tu Yuanwei, Gao Wei, Daxing Zhuang and other wei in the west of the county have been broken by bandits in more than twenty places, and about dozens of li have been burned.

More than 500 civilians have been killed or injured, and Yanghe, Zhenglou, and Linheji and other places are also in imminent danger. The county party headquarters and the district and town heads have jointly telegraphed the provincial government and the Department of Civil Affairs, requesting that a large army be sent to suppress [the bandits].

Nantong 89

Military and police jointly suppress bandits in the Qi'an District: Liu Ying of the Fifth Division and the Thirteenth Company of the Provincial Police Corps jointly suppressed bandits in the Qi'an District on the 8th. They surrounded and suppressed a gang of bandits towards Xinglong Town in three routes. The two sides fought fiercely for three hours, killing more than ten bandits and capturing thirty bandits including Cao Zhang alive. Four soldiers and policemen were injured, and Wang Chengjian, a soldier of the Provincial Police Corps, was killed in action. The bandits captured on the 9th were sent to the Clearing and Suppression Headquarters for interrogation.

Rugao 90

Robbery and injury case near the city: At the Zhuang locality, about ten li west of the city,

at about 1 pm the day before yesterday, more than two hundred bandits suddenly came, each holding a Mauser pistol and a flashlight, firing shots as a show of force and engaging in wanton robbery, and shooting dead many members of the Zhang family, a widow. The bandits only roared away at about 4 pm, and the loss was no less than tens of thousands of gold.

Xu Jiajin sentenced to two years of imprisonment: Xu Jiajin, a party member and former party newspaper editor in this county, was arrested and sent to the Jiangsu High Court for trial on suspicion of involvement with the Communist Party. More than a year has passed since then, and there has been no verdict. It is now learned that Xu Jiajin has been sentenced to two years of imprisonment for counter-revolutionary crimes.

Pinghu 91

Shenzhen Robbery and Injury Case: Ni Liuxiang from Nanda Tongqiao, Shenzhen Zhen, is a family with a modest income. At midnight on the 7th, more than ten robbers suddenly came, speaking in the local dialect and the dialect of Jiangbei, with torches and sticks, smashing the gate and

entering, immediately tying up Ni's entire family and looting wantonly. Liuxiang was burned by the bandits with洋燭, the suffering was unbearable to see. At that time, the wife of Chen, a certain timber merchant from Xinpu Town, happened to be a guest at Ni's house and was also robbed of more than 300 yuan in cash. As a result, the total loss was about a thousand yuan. At the same time, the house of Shen Axin in the north of Shen was also robbed, and more than one hundred yuan in clothing, newspapers, jewelry, and cash were robbed.

Huzhou 92

Bandits kidnap and set fires: At Changqiao, about a li from Heping Town, Changxing,

residents Xu Aliuyi and Xu Guiqing are families with modest incomes and are coveted by bandits. A few days ago, they received letters from bandits demanding huge sums of money. Because each family ignored them, more than ten bandits suddenly came at about 10 am on the 6th and kidnapped Xu Guiqing. At about 12 pm on the same day, more than twenty robbers came again, each holding a wooden-cased gun and a flashlight, and carrying incendiary

items, setting fire to all the houses of Xu Aliuyi's family.

Jiaxing 93

County citizens petition to suppress rice prices: The price of rice in Jiaxing has risen to 16 yuan per dan, and the black market price has even risen to more than 16 yuan, and there is still a tendency to continue to rise. Some unscrupulous merchants are taking this opportunity to hoard and speculate. If this continues, the people's food will be worrying. Therefore, Huang Tongsheng, Zhao Changzhao, Xu Jinjian, and Zhang Peng, citizens of this county, jointly submitted a petition to the County Party Department and the County Government yesterday to suppress rice prices, and to send personnel to purchase foreign rice and transport it to Jiaxing for sale at a fair price to provide relief. It is not yet known how the authorities will handle this matter.

Maintenance of Order

Due to the final performances in the past two days, the audience was extremely crowded, and there was no room to stand in each ballpark. In order to maintain order, the association sent party boy scouts to stand in the venue, and the military and police maintained order everywhere outside the venue. Due to the large number of people, it was inevitable that disputes would occur. Fearing that the original military and police might not be able to handle them, a joint military and police inspection office was temporarily established. In addition, in the event of disputes or accidents, the military and police in the venue would take the perpetrators to the disciplinary office for persuasion or warning to avoid disturbing public order.

Yesterday's Finals Details 98

Men's Basketball

Tianjin Wins the Championship

Thirty-Eight to Twenty-Three Victory over Shanghai

Tianjin's Five Tigers Display Great Power

Shanghai Struggles Under Encirclement in the First Half

Yao En Han Scores Seven Goals Alone

Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, the men's basketball finals were held. The Tianjin and Shanghai teams competed for the championship. Drawn by the renowned reputations of both teams, spectators packed the basketball court, leaving no space. Tianjin initially fielded the Nan Rund Kai five tigers. Shanghai's lineup consisted of Huang Yunli and Liang Guoquan as forwards, He Tong as center, and Wang Jinpeng and Lu Zhongen as guards. Midway through the game, Tianjin's right guard, Wang Xiliang, sustained a foot injury and was replaced by He Buyun. From the start, the Shanghai team was consistently trapped and unable to make progress. Huang Yunli and Liang Guoquan could not even get close to the basket. Tang Baokun first scored a point from a free throw, opening the record. Although Shanghai tried hard to defend, they were no match for the five tigers' onslaught. Tang Baokun was especially active, constantly making it difficult for the opponents to anticipate his moves. The score at the end of the first half was:

Seventeen to Four, Tianjin wins. Shanghai's four points came from Liang Guoquan and Lu Zhongen each making a free throw, and He Tong scoring a field goal.

After the break, the teams switched sides and Shanghai changed its lineup again, with Wei Haiqing as center and Tan Dahua replacing Huang Yunli as right forward. At the start, the Shanghai team was still flustered. Tan Dahua was also not having much success. Tianjin's Liu Jianchang made a point from a free throw, opening the record. After that, the game remained closely contested for a while. Shanghai seemed to be gaining momentum slightly. At that time, Kong Guangyi had replaced Wang Jinpeng as right forward and also scored a field goal. Tianjin immediately called a timeout, bringing Yao En Han, the Far Eastern star, in place of Wei Pengyun. The Tianjin team was like taking a shot of morphine, their spirits revived. Yao En Han, with his long-range shots and close-range attacks, did not miss. He scored six goals alone,

and one point from a free throw. Together with Tang Baokun, they were truly a great partnership. Tianjin right guard,

Wang Xiliang, also entered the game with an injury. Shanghai relied solely on Kong Guangyi to fight, but one hand cannot clap. However, in the second half, the Shanghai team played better and was able to handle everything. If they had this spirit in the first half, the score would not have been so far apart. The score for the second half was twenty-one to nineteen, Tianjin wins. The total score was thirty-eight to twenty-three. The men's basketball championship thus went to Tianjin.

Women's Basketball

Pingxing Wins the Championship 101

丨Peiping and Shanghai Jia Each Score Twenty-Four Points丨

The Scores Are Equal

The Winner Is Decided by Throwing the Ball

Peiping Throws Ten Field Goals and Four Free Throws

Shanghai Jia Throws Nine Field Goals and Six Free Throws

丨Shanghai Unfortunately Loses the Championship丨

Evenly Matched

Shanghai Women's Basketball Team

(Photographed by Wang Kai)

Yesterday afternoon at 3:30 PM, in the women's basketball finals, Shanghai Jia played against the Peiping team. The Peiping players were tall and strong, and their shots were more powerful than Shanghai's. Shanghai, on the other hand, excelled in lively passing. The two sides were evenly matched, and the game was extremely fierce. In the first quarter, the score was five to six, with Peiping winning. In the second quarter, the Shanghai team launched a major counterattack, with forward Chen Yingrui standing out in particular. As a result, the score was three to five, with Shanghai winning. The total score for the first half was ten to nine, with Shanghai winning by only one point. The Peiping team suffered from inaccurate free throws.

Final Struggle

In the second quarter, the two sides fought even more fiercely, and the scores were very close, constantly differing by only one or two points. The audience's cheers shook the earth. The result of the third quarter was seven to five, with Shanghai winning. At that time, the total score was seventeen to fourteen, with Shanghai winning. In the fourth quarter, the two sides made their final struggle. Shanghai's famous player Chen Yingrui went in and out of the game, continuously scoring two goals. The audience all thought that Shanghai had hope. Unexpectedly, Peiping's center Huang Shushen displayed her divine power, scoring six points in a row. As such, the two sides held each other until the final whistle,

announcing the end of the game. The scoreboard showed twenty-four to twenty-four. The scores were equal. But according to the rules of women's basketball, there is no overtime. If the scores are equal, the number of field goals made should be used as the deciding factor. After checking the scorebook, the result was that Peiping had thrown ten field goals and Shanghai had nine. Therefore, the victory was awarded to Peiping. The women's basketball championship was ultimately taken by Peiping. Shanghai can truly be said to be unfortunate.

Men's Volleyball

Guangdong Wins the Championship 103

丨Yesterday Two to One Victory over Hong Kong丨

Competition Was Quite Intense

The Guangdong and Hong Kong teams held the men's volleyball championship finals at 1:00 PM on the 10th. The audience reached 3,000 people, extremely crowded. The fierce battle lasted two hours.

The once-famous Hong Kong team was defeated by Guangdong by a score of one to two. The competition is briefly recorded below.

Hong Kong Volleyball Team That Lost to Guangdong Yesterday

(Guangdong Team Seen in Yesterday's Newspaper)

(Photographed by Chunghwa)

Hong Kong Takes the Lead

At 3:15 PM, the members of the two teams entered the field in uniform, performing some warm-up exercises. When the time arrived, the referee blew the whistle, and the fierce battle began. Hong Kong's Zou Bingxin served the ball and scored two points in a row, opening the record. Guangdong suffered a setback at the start. The Hong Kong team then gained another four points, making the score four to zero. Their momentum was overwhelming.

Everyone Is Cautious 104

However, the Guangdong team did not lose heart due to this small setback. The spirit of the entire team was invigorated.

The front and middle row partnerships attacked smoothly and scored three points. At this point, the competition between the two sides became increasingly fierce. Moreover, their strengths were evenly matched, and everyone was cautious, not daring to be negligent. It was extremely difficult to make progress. After a long stalemate, Hong Kong maintained its advantage, completing the formation with a score of eleven to three.

Full Counterattack 105

At that time, the audience felt that the Hong Kong team was sure to win. Unexpectedly, Guangdong suddenly launched a full-scale counterattack. Li Lianying in the front row repeatedly displayed his rapid smashes, which were able to hit the target every time. As a result, the score gradually increased, making the proportion eight to eleven. The morale of the army was boosted.

Hong Kong's Formation Shakes 106

Seeing that the enemy's momentum was strong, Hong Kong's formation gradually became chaotic. Moreover, because they were too eager, they gave the opponent an opportunity to take advantage of. Guangdong pressed harder and harder. Before long, they suddenly turned the tables and won with a score of eighteen to fifteen. Although the Hong Kong team struggled to catch up, it was difficult to do so. The first game ended in defeat with a score of seventeen to twenty-one.

Shanghai Tennis Players (Right) Kuai Shuping 107

(Left) Li Lian

Photographed by Lin Zeren of the Photography Society

Winning Applause

After a few minutes of rest, the game continued, and the fighting between the two sides became even more intense. The performance was very exciting, winning a lot of applause from the audience. The three players in Guangdong's middle row smashed the ball effectively, winning many points. Progress was made evenly, and it was difficult to tell the difference. Suddenly, the Hong Kong team led again with a score of eleven to nine. After changing sides,

Hong Kong's Chen Xibing served the ball and scored four points in a row. After several more exchanges,

they won with a score of twenty-one to eighteen. The two teams each won one game.

Decisive Key 108

The third game was the key to the final victory and the championship. Therefore, both sides spared no effort to compete. Chen Xibing, a strong player from the Hong Kong team, repeatedly used his smashing skills in the hope of killing the enemy. However, the Guangdong side's front row guarding skills were very good, and it was difficult to succeed. The scores rose and fell, following each other closely. After each team reached eighteen, the Guangdong team succeeded in serving three times, winning the final victory. The volleyball championship was thus won by Guangdong.

Women's Tennis

Tianjin Wins the Championship 116

丨Three to Two Victory over Shanghai丨

Tianjin Wins Two Singles Groups and One Doubles Group

Shanghai Wins One Singles Group and Unfortunately Fails

The Liang Sisters Are Really Impressive

Kuai Shuping Is Impatient and Therefore Fails 117

(1) The Doubles Battle

In the women's tennis finals, Tianjin played against Shanghai. Two singles matches had been completed on the 9th, with Tianjin and Shanghai each winning one group. Tianjin's Liang Peiyao won against Shanghai's Kuai Shuping two to zero. Shanghai's Li Lian won against Tianjin's Liang Peiyu two to zero. Yesterday morning's doubles match had a significant impact on the third and fourth singles matches. The game started at 9:00 AM. The Liang sisters flew horizontally and vertically, with superb skills. They won Shanghai's Li Lian and Kuai Shuping in two sets with scores of six to four and six to three.

Referee Hao Boyang

Winning Situation

Shanghai's Kuai Shuping served first, followed by Tianjin. Shanghai won two games in a row at the start, with great momentum. Li Lian served, and although Tianjin won one game, Shanghai won again on the backhand. Tianjin quickly caught up, making it a three-three draw, and then a

four-four draw. Li and Kuai gradually revealed panic after winning first and then drawing. They lost two games in a row. The Liang sisters then won the first set with six to four.

Continuing to fight, Shanghai served, and Tianjin lost two games in a row again. Peiyu and Peiyao remained calm and unhurried, making it a two-two draw, and then a three-three draw. After that, Shanghai gradually became tired, and Kuai Shuping was exhausted from running around, making it difficult to defend.

Tianjin waited for work while Shanghai worked, winning three games in a row, and then winning the second set with six to three　　Tianjin's Victory

Tianjin's ability to win against Shanghai can be described as follows: (1) They were unhurried and calm. Although they lost two games in a row at the beginning, their attitude remained calm. When the enemy became flustered, they seized the opportunity to advance. (2) They were able to take advantage of the enemy's weaknesses. Shanghai's Li Lian connected the ball quite steadily, which was very risky. However, Kuai Shuping hit the ball too fiercely and was too impatient, so the ball often fell in front of the net or flew out of bounds. Tianjin took advantage of this weakness and desperately hit the ball towards Kuai, so that Li Lian had no chance to get the ball. As a result, Kuai Shuping was exhausted, and Li Lian could not support it alone, losing again and again. Tianjin then won.

(2) The Singles Battle

In women's tennis, Tianjin had already won one singles and one doubles group. In the afternoon, in the second singles group,

Tianjin's Liang Peiyu won against Shanghai's Kuai Shuping again, one group six to two, two to six,

eight to six. Shanghai's Li Lian won against Tianjin's Liang Peiyao in one group, three to six, six to zero, six to three. Tianjin still won the championship with a score of three to two.

Hong Kong Team That Won the Swimming Championship Yesterday

Photographed by Wang Kai

Chinese swimming is extremely underdeveloped, and its results are far behind. This time it was held in Hangzhou, using the Zhijiang University swimming pool. The pool did not have a hot water pipe, and the spring was extremely cold, so the difference in results was natural and should not be blamed on the selection.

However, the rise of swimming athletes in Liaoning was unexpected. Shi Xinglong's long-distance swimming is well-known. It is said that Shi's younger brother, Shi Xingzhi, is good at short-distance swimming and is famous in Dalian. If he could have come this time, Liaoning would have won the championship in eight or nine out of ten cases. Shi Xinglong is used to long-distance swimming, but the Zhijiang swimming pool is too small. Shi is not used to turning around while swimming, so his results were poor. This is also a shortcoming of the conference. Guangdong's swimming results were slightly worse, and the absence of relay swimming

further reduced the team's color. Shanghai did not even get a seat except for relay swimming, which was unexpected.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Party Department Welcomes All Athletes

Photographed by Wang Kai

Closing Ceremony Today

The Ceremony and Awards Will Be Held at 2:00 PM This Afternoon 119

The National Games, which opened to this day, has reached its end. It was originally scheduled to close on the 10th, but due to the heavy rain on the 8th, it was extended by one day. The closing ceremony and awards ceremony had to be postponed to 2:00 PM this afternoon at the track and field.

Closing Order

Closing Ceremony Order: (1) Take seats, (2) All stand at attention, (3) Play music, (4) All bow three times to the Party, the National Flag, and the portrait of the Prime Minister, (5) The chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will, (6) The president delivers a speech, (7) The representative of the Central Party Department delivers a speech,

(8) Representatives from various provinces, cities, and overseas Chinese groups deliver speeches, (9) Speeches, (10) Awards, (11) Photography, (12) Entertainment, (13) Closing.

Chairman Has Been Determined

Dai Jitao, the president of the conference, is very enthusiastic about this conference. In addition to personally attending the conference every day, Dai always made lengthy speeches at the conferences that welcomed the athletes to encourage them. When the conference opened, Dai came to Hangzhou from Beijing overnight to participate. Therefore, unless there are important matters, Dai will still come to Hangzhou to preside over the closing ceremony and awards ceremony.

Distribution of Awards

This conference sought awards from various places, with more than 3,000 types, countless silver shields, silver banners, silver cups, and silver tripods. Other items such as towels, bathrobes, handkerchiefs, ties, and silk woven scenery, were luxurious and gorgeous, piled up in many rooms. Therefore, the committee spent a lot of effort on the distribution of awards, planning day and night. It is estimated that it will only be completed this morning, otherwise it may be too late for the awards ceremony.

Taking a Car to Transfer to Shanghai

After the awards ceremony this afternoon, the reception team has discussed with the Road Bureau to add more than 20 cars for the return of the athletes to avoid congestion. They will return to Shanghai on the early train tomorrow morning to participate in the welcome meetings of various schools in Shanghai.

Rushing to Finish

The conference has a thousand ends and ten thousand threads, and it took half a year to prepare before it could be established. Today, in the blink of an eye, the conference is coming to an end. The chairman stipulated that the matters of each group should be completed by the end of April. Therefore, the staff who have worked hard will have just finished the meeting affairs and will have to rush to finish the closing matters.

The Feng Yong University football and basketball teams from Fengtian participated in the National Games held in Hangzhou this time. They set off from Fengtian on the 23rd of last month. Now that the competition is over, they are scheduled to return to Fengtian on the Fengtian Maru on the 13th of this month. More than 50 athletes from Anhui arrived in Shanghai from Hangzhou yesterday. Assorted Snippets 121

Regret of Missing Out: Yesterday's basketball and volleyball games were packed with spectators even before the matches started. Those who couldn't find seats resorted to climbing on wooden structures or clinging to pillars, an overwhelming number. A group of students from a certain girls' school arrived on time, only to find no space left, resulting in their regret. One of the students jokingly said to her classmates, "Our intention wasn't sincere enough today, leading to our punishment of facing the wall."

Overheated People: The last few scenes were the most exciting. Yesterday, the temperature in Hangzhou suddenly rose, and the audience's enthusiasm also surged with the weather. The biggest sufferers were the children, squeezed into the crowd, unable to see or move. Around 3 o'clock, two children had already fainted from the heat in the basketball court. Additionally, a middle-aged man collapsed on the ground. Both were carried out by the municipal hospital ambulance team for treatment. It was reported that there were over ten similar fainting incidents in various venues due to the scorching sun and unbearable atmosphere.

Legal Trouble: In the southeast corner of the basketball court, two young men started fighting over standing space. One was punched red near his left eye and argued relentlessly. Despite police mediation, they continued to brawl and were taken out of the venue together and sent to the police station for investigation. Getting into legal trouble for watching a lively event is not worth it.

Like Vermicelli Dots: The audience around the volleyball court formed a square shape, resembling a face, with the net in the middle like a line, and the ball like a dot. If Dr. Zhang Feng, the inventor of the Shape-Number Character Method, were to see this, he would surely boast about his "vermicelli dot" method.

Promoting Foreign Goods: The Quaker Oats Company sent coupons to players, coaches, and referees, entitling them to a free serving of Quaker Oats at the Hangzhou YMCA Western restaurant. The coupon stated that it had nourishing and health-promoting effects.

Promoting Domestic Goods: The Shanghai and Hangzhou Joint Association of Domestic Goods Factories held a mobile exhibition in Hangzhou this time. They also had preferential measures for athletes from various provinces. Those wearing athlete badges on these two days (today and tomorrow) could sign their names and draw a lot. Each lot had a domestic goods gift, with the largest being domestic wool and cloth, and the smallest being domestic candies and toothpaste. The efforts of those promoting domestic goods are commendable.

A Small Token: The Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Provincial Party Department, noting the gathering of athletes from afar, hosted them in the grand hall last night. Besides speeches and performances, each person received a bag of refreshments and a package of Hangzhou local products. It was said that the contents of the local product package, such as tea, silk fabrics, and scenery items, were worth about two silver dollars each, totaling more than 1,900 packages distributed.

Emptied Out: The Games are scheduled to close today, so the athletes will only stay in Hangzhou for one night. Yesterday afternoon, they rushed to the money storage to withdraw their deposits. The amounts were minimal, and they bought local products in the market to take home.

Hosting National Games Athletes 123

The Shanghai Special Municipality Education Bureau and the World Chinese Students' Federation initiated a joint effort with various renowned universities and cultural organizations in the city to hold a meeting on April 13th (Sunday) at 1:00 PM at the Central Auditorium on North Sichuan Road, Yokohama Bridge, to welcome athletes from all districts attending the National Games. The preparations for this event have been reported in this newspaper. It is now known that the organizations and schools that newly joined the effort yesterday include the College of Commerce of Central University, Guanghua University, Shanghai Law School, The Commercial Press, China Bookstore, Shanghai YMCA, etc. Invitation letters to athletes from all districts were sent to Hangzhou yesterday morning via express mail. At 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, representatives from various organizations and schools held the second preparatory meeting at the Hua An Building, 8th floor. Those present included Peng Shikun from Guanghua University, Hua Panzhu from Jiaotong University, Xu Xinyi from the Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association, Luo Qingbin from Tongji University, Chuan Xunren from Jinan University, Ling Xitao from the Shanghai YMCA, Chen Xianmo from the College of Commerce of Central University, Jin Guangmei and Huang Juying from Shanghai Law School, Zhu Weiyun from The Commercial Press, Qi Yun from Fudan University, Fei Zifei from the Pharmacy Department of Sino-French University, Pan Runfu and Jiang Henglin from Shanghai College of Political Science and Law, Zhao Ziyi from China Bookstore, Zhu Shaoping and Zhu Shaozhang from the World Chinese Students' Federation, and others, totaling more than ten people. Chairman Zhu Shaoping reported on the progress of the preparations, followed by discussions on various items. The following resolutions were made: (1) Each university should appoint ten teachers and students to serve as hosts. (2) The hosting activities should be divided into two groups: one group will host at the North and South train stations, and the other group will go to Songjiang to welcome the athletes arriving by train. Today (the 11th), the hosting duties will be carried out by Jiaotong University and the Law School. In the next two days, the duties will be divided among other schools. (3) The resident general host at the North Station will be the World Chinese Students' Federation during the day and the YMCA after 6:00 PM. The Commercial Press, China Bookstore, and the YMCA will send personnel to host the night trains. (4) Banners and other items for the hosts should be prepared by the World Chinese Students' Federation. (5) The YMCA will be responsible for contacting and coordinating the resident hosting office at the North Station. (6) The performances by various schools should be novel and truly exciting. Currently, in addition to the martial arts performance by the Jingwu Athletic Association, there will be a Western music ensemble by Jinan University and a short play (Winning the Championship) by Shanghai College of Political Science and Law. At 5:00 PM this afternoon, the hosts appointed by each school will hold a meeting at the World Chinese Students' Federation at 95 Carter Road to discuss the hosting methods for the next two days.

News Briefs

Dr. Ma Guli's Lecture at Nanzhong

Dr. Ma Guli, a special commissioner sent by the French Ministry of Education to investigate higher education in China, delivered a lecture at the auditorium of Nanzhong First Academy at 3:00 PM on the 9th at the invitation of Principal Zhang of Nanzhong. The French consul, guests from central party and government agencies, and faculty and students of the school, totaling over a thousand people, attended. First, Principal Zhang Jingqiu of Nanzhong gave a welcoming speech, saying that Dr. Ma Guli not only speaks Chinese but also has a deep understanding of Chinese literature, which is admirable. Then, Dr. Ma Guli took the stage and spoke in Chinese without translation, saying that although he studied Chinese language and literature in Paris, he lacked experience and feared that he would not be able to understand many things, and asked for forgiveness. He expressed his deep desire to discuss academic research with ambitious people and young students, but with so many topics, he didn't know where to start. He then spoke about important issues related to China and Europe, namely, the research of Sinology in European countries. Europeans have been studying Chinese Sinology for a long time. During the Liang Dynasty, Europeans traveled to China and returned with notes and various research findings, but they were still in the preliminary stage. There was further progress in the late Ming and early Qing dynasties. In the sixteenth, seventeenth, and eighteenth centuries, many scholars of literature, philosophy, politics, and economics produced and published works. In the nineteenth century, there were countless books on Chinese literature, such as philosophy and history, showing the extent of European research on Chinese literature. Europeans have translated many Chinese literary books, and their research achievements continue to this day. Many European countries have Chinese schools to study Chinese literature, especially France. There are four places to study Chinese literature in Paris, France: (1) the School of Oriental Languages, (2) the Chinese Language School, (3) the University of Paris, and (4) the French Academy. In addition, there are Chinese libraries and research societies. The Oriental Language Library is rich in famous Chinese books. In addition to the six public libraries in France that study Chinese, there are also three private libraries. French Sinologists and professors teaching French to Chinese students can easily understand and achieve twice the result with half the effort. Chinese figures like Wu Zhihui and Li Shizeng have all studied in France. The United Kingdom and Germany also study Chinese literature. London has the School of Oriental Languages and the Cambridge Library, which also has a rich collection of books. Berlin, Germany, has the School of Oriental Languages, and the library also has a large collection of books. Their universities also have Chinese professors teaching Sinology. In addition, countries such as Italy, Rome, Poland, and the Netherlands are studying Chinese literature, and their progress will undoubtedly be greater. Many European scholars of Chinese literature have translated classics such as the Thirteen Classics dozens of times (except for the Gongyang Commentary, which has not been translated), philosophical works such as the Tao Te Ching have been translated seventy-three times, and Zhuangzi, Liezi, Lu's Springs and Autumns, Mozi, Huainanzi, and Xunzi have all been translated. Historical books such as A Comprehensive Mirror for Aid in Government and Sima Qian's Records of the Grand Historian have all been translated into French. Collections such as the Eight Great Masters of Tang and Song prose have not been completely translated, and only a portion of literary history has been translated. More than 400 poems by Du Fu have been translated by the British, and there are also translations of poems by Li Bai. In addition, the main points of Chinese culture, poetry, lyrics, novels, Romance of the Three Kingdoms, Journey to the West, and Dramatical Ballads have all been translated. In addition to translating the above-mentioned books, Europeans plan to translate the complete history of China and have already begun translating a history of the Five Dynasties of China. The above is a general overview of the research on Sinology in various European countries. The reason why Europeans want to study Chinese Sinology is that China was the earliest civilization, and the ancient texts of more than 4,000 years have considerable value. In the minds and needs of Europeans, there is great interest in research. From my observation, Chinese culture is like the recent progress in industry and commerce. China is an ancient civilized country, and Europe is a newly advanced country in terms of material things. China has adopted some of it, and Europeans also deeply admire Chinese culture. The so-called exchange of spiritual civilization and material civilization has a profound impact on the international future. Finally, Principal Zhang gave a speech of thanks, saying that the French consul changed the date of his lecture because everyone had been sitting for a long time. The meeting ended at about 4 o'clock.

Suzhou Boy Scout Jamboree News 124

Camp Office Starts Work

Since the Jiangsu Boy Scout Association began preparing for the jamboree, all comrades have been invigorated and working harder. The prices of these items were assessed one by one yesterday. Other food items were carefully selected for quality, and their prices were lower than those in the town market. Local News

City Executive Committee Convenes 127

Clearance Day Commemoration Assembly

Tomorrow morning at 9:00 AM at the Penglai Grand Theater. Tomorrow (the 12th) is the third anniversary of the Chinese Kuomintang's purge of the Communist Party. The Shanghai Special City Executive Committee has decided to convene an assembly at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 12th at the Penglai Grand Theater on Penglai Road in the South City, summoning representatives from various agencies, organizations, schools, and party departments at all levels to attend. The City Propaganda Department has prepared a large number of propaganda materials, ready to be distributed within the assembly.

In order to enable all comrades and people from all walks of life in the city to have a deep understanding of the significance of the "Purification Day" and to facilitate propaganda, the City Training Department has widely distributed a thick volume on the "Purification Movement". People from all districts, branches, agencies, public organizations, and walks of life in the city may request a copy from the Party Member Training Section of the department. The book is divided into three parts, totaling two hundred thousand words. The first chapter is "The Fallacies of Communism and the Rebellion of Action", containing four articles. The second chapter is "The Course and Propositions of the Purification", containing three articles. The third chapter is "The Necessary Understanding After the Purification", containing three articles. The content is quite rich and the analysis is particularly detailed.

Purification Commemoration

Inspection of Pedestrians in the Chinese Area 128

To be implemented starting today

Director Yuan of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, in view of April 12 being the "Purification Day", stated that prevention cannot be taken lightly. In addition to coordinating with the concession authorities for joint defense measures and mutual assistance, large-scale inspections will be carried out at various key points starting today. Inspectors dispatched by the bureau will supervise the police officers in each district to inspect pedestrians.
