Women's Life

Melancholy Female Poet: Baihe 206

Yu Yan's "Lake Wind"

One evening, at a coffee shop in Ximen, I saw a "Creative Monthly Review" in a magazine. The last paragraph was a critique of Ms. Yu Yan's collection of poems, "Lake Wind."

What kind of message does the female poet Yu Yan, who is making her debut on the literary scene, bring us in her collection "Lake Wind"? It's a melancholic lake wind, a sorrowful sentiment. Her emotions are not commensurate with her age; a pessimistic and world-weary tone has grown in her young heart. Objectively speaking, her profound melancholy is not entirely due to the stimulation of actual life, but is also somewhat influenced by pessimistic philosophy.

Before reading "Lake Wind," I already had the impression of "a melancholy female poet" in my mind.

Opening the collection, I saw in the preface evaluative words such as "Yan's poems are indeed too bleak," which immediately reminded me of the lines in Li Daoqing's "Qingyu Case Ci":

Now I understand, spring sorrow and hatred, are always the poet's lot.

I remember someone saying that women are creatures rich in emotion, and poets are also rich in emotion, so it can be said that they are "women among men" (see Kitamura Tokoku's "World-Weary Poets and Women"). Considering the meaning of these words,

then it can be concluded that women have a special talent for writing poetry, which may not be without reason. However, opponents argue that poetry is a symbol of human suffering. Chinese women have traditionally lived in a dependent position due to social structures. Unless they are abandoned or widowed, they will not have much suffering. Moreover, they do not come into contact with human life.

What they know is nothing more than needlework and cosmetics; what they feel is nothing more than spring flowers, autumn moons, and the bedchamber. Their poverty is sometimes physical hardship, but there is no spiritual pain. Or sometimes there are a few with clear minds, but they are bound by the ethics of the family, and they disappear in a moment. Therefore, it is rare to have remarkable literary creations.

Regardless of the literary value of Yu Yan's "Lake Wind," I will now just write a few personal thoughts after reading it.

"Lake Wind" contains a total of thirty-eight poems, twenty-two of which describe scenery, fourteen express emotions, and two are miscellaneous small poems. Among the landscape poems, "A Broken Boat" best fits the form of a pure narrative poem, while "Nameless Flower" is the most brilliant. Among the lyric poems, although many use objects to convey emotions, we can also glimpse a bit of the author's thoughts.

Two-thirds of the lines in "Lake Wind" are negative in meaning. In almost every poem, one can read phrases related to a state of melancholy, such as "loneliness of life," "sorrowful sentiment," "heart after being wounded,"

"night cry of the cuckoo," "infinite sorrow," "skeleton in the grave," "withered yellow leaves," "sad new moon," "final annihilation," and so on. According to the research of abnormal psychologists, the number of Chinese women who are physically weak and mentally depressed is quite large, especially among women in the intellectual class. Because of their weak constitution and mental depression, they usually feel listless and tired.

When they encounter relatively strong stimuli, they feel overwhelmed, unbearable, helpless, and without a plan, and even become "languid" or "sick," and "thinner than a yellow flower." Therefore, their expressions of emotion are mostly depressed.

Words such as worry, sorrow, and weeping, hidden behind closed doors, have become meaningful activities in the daily life of poets (see Pan Guangdan's "Analysis of Xiaoqing"). The above discussion is just a conclusion drawn after a general observation of female poets in the old Chinese era, and can also be regarded as a diagnosis for "sentimental and sickly" female poets.

Whether the author of "Lake Wind" has the mental depression mentioned above, we dare not make any conjectures because we do not know "Yan's experiences" and "the marks on her heart." But in her few lyric poems, if those lines are all the author's confessions and expressions, we can cite the following lines confessed by Ms. Yu:

In "I Wish to Transform into Green Smoke," she tells us her ideals and aspirations. She wants to break away from the human world, which has a "land of aging" and "pain and worry," and transform into green smoke.

Resting in the mountains,

Becoming a confidante of the clouds.

To express her interest, the author also titled herself "Xiuyun" (Cloud Sleeve). Whether this interest is inspired by the author's love of nature or influenced by others' pessimistic philosophies, we do not need to study it. But we can say that the author's view of life is world-weary. Let us try to read her following lines:

Ah, the beautiful dewdrops on the lotus petals,

Life is as empty as you are.

Although people will sometimes praise you,

Do not be greedy for that fleeting vanity.

When the sunlight shines brightly on the earth,

You will be greatly shamed and ridiculed.

/ Summer Night

Let us drink a glass of sweet red wine,

Do not seek people's pity,

People's pity,

Is more shameful than sneers.

/ To Ms. SS

A heart that is bright red and passionate,

Is deeply trapped in this empty life.

It's all over,

What is success and hope,

What is true affection and sincere love,

Are all buried in the desolate valley,

Submerged in the Dead Sea.

/ A Dirge of Life

Reading these lines, I thought of Mr. Qian Xingcun's saying that "a pessimistic and world-weary tone has grown in her young heart," which seems very reasonable. Disgust for the world is originally a common trait among young people, especially among poets. Originally, in the career of mankind,

since the germination of thought, everyone hopes for truth, beauty, and goodness, and dislikes ugliness. This is a natural principle. But for people who are not familiar with the world and cannot penetrate the depths of the world, when they first encounter all the disturbances and disharmony of the real world, they feel that everything is at odds with their ideals. In the youth age when knowledge and experience are in opposition, and ideals and reality are at war, it is natural to have strange and world-weary views of life. Because of her young age and the fact that she has not lost the pure thoughts of her girlhood, the author of "Lake Wind" is completely isolated from the real social life, and it is inevitable that she will have a world-weary view of life.

Since a poet has developed a disgust for actual life, he dares not expect too much hope for the future. Therefore, he has to think back to the illusions of the past and savor the taste of olives in remembrance. Therefore, the author of "Lake Wind" often sings about her childhood.

Where is the perfect dreamland?

In this past childhood.

/ A Dirge of Life

And afraid to see

The neighbors laughing at me

Leaning on the chests of those old people

I am not |

I am not tired of that pure sound

Jealous of the innocence of the children |

Because my childhood is hard to come back

/ Me in May

But these are not the author's true distresses,

Nor are they her true sorrows. What exactly is the melancholy and distress of Ms. Yu Yan? We can find the root cause in these lines:

Sickness,

Depression,

Let the window,

Be battered by wind and rain,

Who will comfort me?

/ Sick

Ask,

The vast sky,

This defect in the heart,

What

/ Night's Groan

The singing of the neighboring girl is faint

I'm afraid she's looking for a confidante

Otherwise, why so melancholy

But me,

I still have to envy you,

You have the courage to look for it,

/ Envy

In the overlapping heads,

She opened her eyes and looked around,

Only feels a vast blackness before her eyes,

Unable to find a confidante

Even more unable to see a companion,

/ A Singer in the City

Ah, wise and intelligent readers, do you all know now the source of our female poet's melancholy? This source of illness is also commonly infected by general poets. All the songs of all young poets have this kind of melancholy lurking. Try to look at Goethe's most famous lines:

Who has never eaten bread in sorrow,

Who has never wept in the night,

Sitting alone waiting for the morning,

He does not know you, ah, you great power.

What exactly is this great power?

To say it is love. A man in his prime, whose physiology

has matured, who is not hungry and thirsty for women? Because of longing for the beauty of one side of the sky, he tosses and turns and cannot sleep, expressing his worries in poetry, and it is naturally easy to win the tears of sympathy from many readers. Similarly, women must also long for men. So-called spring heart flaring and love born, love unsuccessful and poetry made, that is a natural principle.

Human suffering and melancholy, especially the depressed souls of poets, if they hold deep-rooted world-weary concepts, there is no medicine to cure them. Religious beliefs cannot overcome their world-weariness, and worldly pleasures cannot break their negativity. There is only one treasure that can be used as a symptomatic remedy for those purely ideal young poets, and that is love.

Kitamura Tokoku in "World-Weary Poets and Women"

has a very insightful discussion in one section:

World-weary people have no other hope for the present world. Money and profit are certainly not what they hope for. Even the crown of the Son of Heaven and the wealth and glory of the King of the Road are never hoped for. Therefore, the world-weary are incompatible with the hopes of the present world. However, only love has a secret recipe that can penetrate into the groaning chest of world-weary people. The strangest thing is that they place many hopes in love. The thing called "affection" will not let you be quiet for a moment. As soon as you step in, your heart is always disturbed. Moreover, the world-weary who are most prone to agitation in their lives have suffered setbacks in the realization of society, and are instead conquered by the strange magic of love. At this time, he stands up with his whole body and soul and becomes a slave to love. Isn't that a very obvious reason?

Only after men and women love each other can they begin to understand the truth of society. At that time, even a tiny insect is not isolated, nor can it leave us and act automatically. In the society where human beings gather together, we must rely on each other and embrace each other before we can maintain or build society. We cannot understand this principle unless we climb the first level of "loving each other". When a person lives alone, he does not have the elements of a complete member of society. Only after two people come together are they counted as a member of society.

After men and women are united, the floating clouds moving in the sky at dawn also seem to have faces, and the calls of old birds in the forest also seem to have tones. Yesterday's past seems like decades ago, and today's present seems like an existence that can extend for generations.

Since people have gained this proper position, they can understand the obligations to God, the obligations to mankind, and the morality of what they previously thought was a brilliant flower, reducing his delusions and increasing his reality, in order to lay the foundation for him to enter the "noon" of life.

The above discussion can prove that poets in general who have a world-weary view of life are more eager to pursue and be hungry for love than ordinary young men and women. This is something that can often be discovered and confirmed in their literary creations.

Because reading "Lake Wind" gave rise to some thoughts,

I have slipped into saying many irrelevant things. I feel deeply sorry for the author of "Lake Wind" and the readers. Now I should end my words.

Finally, I offer my sincerity, hoping that Ms. Yu Yan will no longer sing such "wandering songs".

That early and late blazing sun,

Also did not warm my heart,

Sorrow and worry,

Often hover in my heart.

Ah, young female poet, turn your strings and change your voice, sing a joyful tune.

Let me wash away the worries of writing,

Let me enjoy your holy light for a long time.

/ Great and Kind Moon: I bless you, melancholy female poet.

New Discoveries on Vitamins by Female Chemists

Recently, two female chemists have made very important discoveries about vitamins. One is Ms. Katherine Hoboe Coward, who is a member of the London Medical Association, and the other is Ms. Vera Rer, a very intelligent scholar in the Department of Biochemistry at Oxford University. The vitamin discovered by Ms. Coward has not yet been named. This vitamin is most abundant in fresh milk, beef, beef liver, and wheat germ, and is an essential nutrient for lambs and mice. But it is not yet known whether it is an essential nutrient for us. Ms. Ritter's contribution to us is vitamin B3. Originally, there was only one type of vitamin B, which was later divided into vitamin B1 and vitamin B2. But now Ms. Ritter has discovered a third type, which is truly good news for researchers in biochemistry. According to Ms. Ritter's experiments, the similarity between vitamin B2 and vitamin B3 is that both are easily destroyed by heat. (Xiong Wan)

Women's Life Submission Guidelines

(1) Articles should focus on discussions of women's issues, news about women at home and abroad, descriptions of women's lives, essays, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Paintings that relate to women's issues are acceptable.

(3) Photos related to women's news, women's issues, and women's lives are acceptable. Individual or group photos are very welcome.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the paper.

(6) Do not write horizontally, and do not write carelessly. Western texts should be omitted if possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw paintings, and do not use colored paper. Black ink must be used on white paper.

(8) Please indicate that submissions should be sent to the Women's Life Department.

(9) Submissions will not be returned whether they are published or not. If a return is required, please state in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration for articles is 3 yuan, 2 yuan, or 1 yuan per thousand words. The same applies to paintings and photos. If there are special articles, the remuneration will be calculated separately.

Ms. Yu Shan

Business News 207

The Dahua Aviation Company announced that it is the first aircraft company in Shanghai, specializing in the sale of commercial and military aircraft. The general manager is Mr. Ernest B. Price, and the deputy general manager is Mr. Mark L. Moody, a well-known figure in the automobile industry in Shanghai. The secretary is lawyer Li Ming. The main office is located in the Dalai House at No. 3 Guangdong Road. The aircraft sold are produced by the American Curtis-Wright Corporation. Prices range from US$7,500 to US$100,000. There are as many as fifteen models available. The capacity varies from three to twenty passengers. An aircraft will be on display within days at the Moody Automobile Company showroom at the corner of Sichuan Road and Avenue Edward VII for public viewing. In addition to selling aircraft, the company also sells Ratto and Curtis automobiles.

It is also heard that Mr. Pan Lansi was formerly the general manager of China Aviation Transportation Co., Ltd. This time, he resigned from his previous position to devote himself to promoting the aviation business and assumed the position of general manager of Dahua Aviation Co., Ltd.

The Sincere Company announced that its silk and satin department on the second floor has ordered no fewer than dozens of varieties of spring silk fabrics from the most famous Swiss factory since last year. A large batch has now arrived.

All goods are displayed on the second floor, including gold and silver thread sparkling voile and georgette printed velvet thin woolen fabrics, which are the most novel. They are light, soft, and smooth, and their colors are bright and elegant. The above varieties are the best. There are also many other fabrics, all of which have never been seen in Shanghai. Therefore, customers have been very enthusiastic recently.

The Mei Yi Food Company announced that it was formerly located on Avenue Edward VII, but due to insufficient space, it moved last month to the Cian Lane at the intersection of Route Paul Beau and Route Lafayette in the French Concession. A new type of almond and lotus seed powder has been invented. The raw materials are pure, nutritious, and rich, and no sugar needs to be added when brewing, so it is very convenient for travelers.

The Dujinsheng Silk Weaving Factory on North Sichuan Road announced that since April 1st, when the spring sale began, all goods have been selling very well. Silk scenery and colorful cotton embroidery are in great demand. In particular, the artistic printed silk ties for 2 yuan per two and the satin ties for 3 yuan per two are the best sellers.

The Dacheng Ginseng Company at the intersection of Lizhuan Road announced that its various ginseng, bird's nest tonics, and supplements are purchased by specialists from authentic sources, so the quality of the goods is better and the price is lower than others. As the construction of the new building has been completed, it will move back to its original location on the 10th of this month to trade in advance and offer special low prices to thank the patronage of customers on weekdays. Tongjilong announced that it is the oldest organization for handling all travel matters. The travel magazine it publishes is also the oldest and most prestigious travel magazine in the world. This firm was founded nearly ninety years ago and has branches all over the world. Its travel magazine is also available in English, French, Italian, Spanish, Dutch, and Danish. The one published in Shanghai

is in English, well-printed, and published quarterly.

This year's summer issue has now been published, and it is believed that aspiring travelers will want to read it first.

The Merlin Advertising Company announced that the "Commercial Firms Directory" is a major annual contribution from the company. It is not only well typeset and printed, but also rich in content. In previous years, a thick volume was published each year. This year, because the internal content has been further expanded, it has been divided into two large volumes. The first volume is dedicated to listing the names of commercial firms in Shanghai, making it very convenient for Shanghai merchants to check. The second volume has now been published, containing merchants from other ports, totaling 48 ports, with more than 5,000 shops. In terms of detail, it is a very satisfactory masterpiece.

Calligraphy and Painting News 208

Wang Jiyuan's European tour farewell commemorative painting exhibition opens this morning at 9:00 AM at the Ningbo Fellow Association on Xizang Road. Many of the painting vouchers issued in advance have been purchased by his friends.

Wang Lianyou from Hangzhou is an artist traveling in Shanghai. People are eager to see his calligraphy, painting, poetry, and literature. He previously toured Hubei and has now returned to Shanghai, residing at the Ningbo Road China Jisheng Society.

Theater News 209

The Paris Grand Theatre announced that the Russian romantic and tragic blockbuster "The Depths of Misery," starring fox star Tears’ Jia Biliwa and three other major Russian stars, is a masterpiece with a lingering and poignant plot.

The scenery is luxurious and magnificent, depicting the imperial Russian officers' abuse of power and the aristocracy's debauchery and extravagance, which is worth watching. The film will be shown at this theater for four consecutive days starting today.

Announcement 210

(1) Please mark all manuscripts sent by commercial firms, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, painters, and doctors as "Shanghai Market Department Received." (2) Please stamp all manuscripts sent by commercial firms, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, painters, and doctors for verification; otherwise, we will not publish them.

(3) A small fee will be paid for long articles on film dramas as usual.
